        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208"><meta property="og:title" content="Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS2 for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/acs.nanolett.3c04208.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="1T-MoS2 has become an ideal anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). However, the metastable feature of 1T-MoS2 makes it difficult to directly synthesize under normal conditions. In addition, it easily transforms into 2H phase via restacking, resulting in inferior electrochemical performance. Herein, the electron configuration of Mo 4d orbitals is modulated and the stable 1T-MoS2 is constructed by nickel (Ni) introduction (1T-Ni-MoS2). The original electron configuration of Mo 4d orbitals is changed via the electron injection by Ni, which triggers the phase transition from 2H to 1T phase, thus improving the electrical conductivity and accelerating the redox kinetics of the material. Consequently,  1T-Ni-MoS2 exhibits superior rate capability (266.8 mAh g–1 at 10 A g–1) and excellent cycle life (358.7 mAh g–1 at 1 A g–1 after 350 cycles). In addition, the assembled Na3V2(PO4)3/C||1T-Ni-MoS2 full cells deliver excellent electrochemical properties and  show great prospects in energy storage devices."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/acs.nanolett.3c04208.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="93187ee97b70075b-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187ee97b70075b-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'a73dfc18-89ed-430d-876b-c6976e22d6be'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187ee97b70075b-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'nano_letters';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/nano_letters/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/nano_letters/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

data-references="https://pubs.acs.org/action/ajaxShowEnhancedAbstract?doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;ajax=true" data-enable-mathjax="true" vocab="http://schema.org/" typeof="ScholarlyArticle" class="article--latest"><div class="figure-viewer"><div class="figure-viewer_row"><div class="figure-viewer_col loop-trap"><div aria-live="polite" aria-atomic="true" class="figure-viewer_modal"><a <script nonce="93187ee97b70075b-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "nalefd";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Electron Configuration Modulation Induced Stabilized 1T-MoS&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; for Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

These metrics are regularly updated to reflect usage leading up to the last few days.</p><p>Citations are the number of other articles citing this article, calculated by Crossref and updated daily.<a href="https://www.crossref.org/services/cited-by/"> Find more information about Crossref citation counts.</a></p><p>The Altmetric Attention Score is a quantitative measure of the attention that a research article has received online. Clicking on the donut icon will load a page at altmetric.com with additional details about the score and the social media presence for the given article. Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/medium/nl3c04208_0006.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> has become an ideal anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). However, the metastable feature of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> makes it difficult to directly synthesize under normal conditions. In addition, it easily transforms into 2H phase via restacking, resulting in inferior electrochemical performance. Herein, the electron configuration of Mo 4d orbitals is modulated and the stable 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> is constructed by nickel (Ni) introduction (1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>). The original electron configuration of Mo 4d orbitals is changed via the electron injection by Ni, which triggers the phase transition from 2H to 1T phase, thus improving the electrical conductivity and accelerating the redox kinetics of the material. Consequently,  1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits superior rate capability (266.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>) and excellent cycle life (358.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 350 cycles). In addition, the assembled Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C||1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> full cells deliver excellent electrochemical properties and  show great prospects in energy storage devices.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D3331%26pageCount%3D8%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DYuxiang%2BZhang%252C%2BJiantao%2BLi%252C%2BXintong%2BLi%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D24%26issueNum%3D11%26contentID%3Dacs.nanolett.3c04208%26title%3DElectron%2BConfiguration%2BModulation%2BInduced%2BStabilized%2B1T-MoS2%2Bfor%2BEnhanced%2BSodium%2BIon%2BStorage%26numPages%3D8%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1530-6984%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dnalefd%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D3338%26publicationDate%3DMarch%2B2024" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2024 UChicago Argonne, LLC., Operators of Argonne National Laboratory. Published by American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291952&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrochemical cells"> Electrochemical cells </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes"> Electrodes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291974&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electronic properties"> Electronic properties </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291688&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Layered materials"> Layered materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290776&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Phase transitions"> Phase transitions </a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=1t-mos2&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_1T-MoS2">1T-MoS<sub>2</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Electron+Configuration+Modulation&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_electron%20configuration%20modulation">electron configuration modulation</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Phase+Transition&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_phase%20transition">phase transition</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode+Material&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode%20material">anode material</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><p class="first">Nowadays, SIBs are attractive for large-scale energy storage due to the inexpensive price and abundant natural resources of sodium element. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7" aria-label="reference 1 to 7">(1−7)</a> However, the inherently heavier molar mass and large ion radius (1.06 Å) of Na<sup>+</sup> often lead to large volume expansion, severe pulverization and sluggish transport kinetics of the electrode materials, yielding reduced reversible capacity and poor cycling performance, which limit their practical application. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 8 and 9">(8,9)</a> It is imminent to explore high-performance electrode materials. The commercial hard carbon anode of SIBs displays relative low capacity, which cannot satisfy the requirements of advanced SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> Therefore, finding new anode materials with outstanding performance has become a research hotspot.</p><p>MoS<sub>2</sub> has gained much study as promising anode materials due to its analogous graphite-like two-dimensional layered structure and high theoretical capacity. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 11 to 14">(11−14)</a> Based on the different coordinated forms of Mo and S atoms, MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits a trigonal prismatic 2H phase and an octahedral coordinated 1T phase. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 15 and 16">(15,16)</a> Under normal conditions, the 4d-orbitals of Mo in 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> divide into d<sub><i>z</i><sup>2</sup></sub>, d<sub><i>x</i><sup>2</sup></sub><sub>–<i>y</i><sup>2</sup></sub>/d<sub><i>xy</i></sub>, and d<sub><i>xz</i></sub>/d<sub><i>yz</i></sub> energy levels. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> The two Mo 4d electrons in 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> fully fill  the lowest d<sub><i>z</i></sub><sup>2</sup> energy level. The 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> demonstrates high structural stability and semiconductor characteristic. Nevertheless, the 4d-orbitals of Mo in 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> split into d<sub><i>xy</i></sub>/d<sub><i>xz</i></sub>/d<sub><i>yz</i></sub> and d<sub><i>z</i><sup>2</sup></sub>/d<sub><i>x</i><sup>2</sup></sub><sub>–<i>y</i><sup>2</sup></sub> energy levels. Due to the incomplete occupation of Mo 4d electrons in the low d<sub><i>xy</i></sub>/d<sub><i>xz</i></sub>/d<sub><i>yz</i></sub> energy levels, the 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> shows metallic  property. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18 ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17 ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 17 to 19">(17−19)</a> Moreover, the distorted octahedral coordination makes 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> have a larger interlayer spacing, which is more favorable for fast Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> At the same time, the not fully filled orbitals cause its thermodynamic unstable nature, making 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> with poor structural stability and hard to directly synthesize under normal conditions, severely limiting its applications.</p><p>Currently, great progress has been achieved to synthesize 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> for improving its sodium storage performance. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref18 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3 ref18 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 3, 18 and 20 to 23">(3,18,20−23)</a> However, there are still inherent limitations, such as difficult control of the reaction and complex synthetic process,  instability of the obtained 1T phase, etc. Therefore, it is necessary to fabricate an innovative and efficient approach to realize transition from 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> to 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>. Nickel is a transition metal element with eight 3d electrons, corresponding to two unpaired 3d electrons. Thus, Ni can easily form a higher valence state by losing unpaired electrons.</p><p>Herein, the electron configuration of Mo 4d orbitals in MoS<sub>2</sub> is modulated by proper Ni introduction via a scalable and facile one-step process, inducing stable 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> (1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>) and achieving the enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> storage property. The Ni element with two unpaired 3d electrons is active to acquire a higher valence state. With the introduction of Ni, the electrons of Ni transfer to the Mo and the local electron configuration of Mo in 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> will be changed and rearranged, leading to the formation of a stable 1T phase. The mechanisms of phase transition and Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance are systematically analyzed via theoretical calculations and experiments. The 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits high electrical conductivity and a lower migration barrier (0.09 eV) of Na<sup>+</sup> than 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (0.73 eV). Meanwhile, the stable 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> delivers high discharged capacity of 644.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, superior rate capability with a capacity of 266.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>. It also demonstrates long cycling properties and maintains 358.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 350 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Moreover, the assembled NVP/C||1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> full cells exhibit the capacity retention of 80% at 5 C beyond 300 cycles.</p><p>A facile one-step synthesis process was employed to obtain 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> nanoflowers, and the corresponding synthesis schematic is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a. The 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> both exhibit typical flower-like morphology (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b, c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>). As shown in high-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) images (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>d),  1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits obvious expanded interlayer spacings (0.95 nm), much larger than the bulk 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (0.62 nm) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>). As shown in the <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>e, f, the hexagonal lattice areas correspond  to 2H phase MoS<sub>2</sub> whereas the trigonal lattice areas  belong to 1T phase, which demonstrate the coexistence of the two phases. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref24 ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21 ref24 ref25" aria-label="reference 21, 24 and 25">(21,24,25)</a> Furthermore, the energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) mappings display the homogeneous dispersion of Mo, S and Ni elements in the obtained sample (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>g).</p><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/medium/nl3c04208_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) Synthesis process of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>. (b) SEM image. (c) TEM image. (d–f) HRTEM images of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> (the inset in f are structure schematics of 2H and 1T phaseof MoS<sub>2</sub>, respectively). (g) EDS mappings of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The X-ray diffraction (XRD) images are presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a. Compared with pure 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub>, a new diffraction peak at 9.3° appears in 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>, which means the formation of 1T phase MoS<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref24 ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21 ref24 ref26" aria-label="reference 21, 24 and 26">(21,24,26)</a> The enlarged interlayer spacing of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> can be attributed to the distorted octahedral coordination of 1T phase, leading to enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> In addition, the peaks of the 1T phase intensify with the increase of the Ni contents (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). The actual Ni contents were tested (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>). In Raman spectra (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b), for 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub>, there are typical characteristic peaks of the E<sub class="stack">2g</sub><sup class="stack">1</sup> and A<sub>1g</sub> modes at about 378.8 and 405.2 cm<sup>–1</sup>. In contrast, new obvious peaks of J<sub>1</sub>, J<sub>2</sub>, E<sub>1g</sub> and J<sub>3</sub> can be observed  in 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> located at 148.5 cm<sup>–1</sup>, 237.8 cm<sup>–1</sup>, 283.5 cm<sup>–1</sup> and 334.7 cm<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, corresponding to 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a></p><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/medium/nl3c04208_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) XRD patterns and (b) Raman spectra of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>. (c) The survey XPS spectrum of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>. (d) Mo 3d spectra and (e) S 2p spectra of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>, respectively. (f) Ni 2p spectra of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>Furthermore,  X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was measured. The survey spectrum of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> sample delivers the coexistences of Mo, S and Ni elements (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>c). The Mo 3d spectra are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d. The 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits two Mo prominent peaks of 3d<sub>3/2</sub> at 232.8 eV and 3d<sub>5/2</sub> at 229.6 eV. For 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>, two new peaks appear at 232.4 and 229.2 eV, indexing to 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18 ref21" aria-label="reference 18 and 21">(18,21)</a> The fitting results show that the 1T phase proportion in 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> is up to 48%. The binding energies of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> are shifted to low values, indicating that the charge density of Mo enhances after Ni electronic injection. In addition, the S 2p spectra exhibit similar shifts (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e). In the Ni 2p spectra of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>f), the peaks around 854.6 and 871.8 eV are assigned to Ni 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Ni 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, respectively, which correspond to Ni<sup>2+</sup>. Residual two peaks located at 857.5 and 875.6 eV correspond to Ni<sup>3+</sup>, demonstrating the successfully incorporation of Ni into the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> simple. Moreover, the satellite peaks can be also observed at 862.4 and 880.1 eV, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28 ref29" aria-label="reference 28 and 29">(28,29)</a></p><p>The Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrodes with different Ni contents was  compared (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>). The 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> with a Ni:Mo molar ratio of 0.02 demonstrates the superior property. For the first cycle, three main cathodic peaks at cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves appeared at 0.99, 0.76 and 0.26 V. The peaks above 0.4 V originate from the intercalation reaction and the formation of solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film. The peak below 0.4 V attributes to the conversion reaction. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> At anodic process, the characteristic peak located at 1.76 V corresponds to the reversible redox process (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> The galvanostatic discharged/charged profiles of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a. The electrode delivers a discharged capacity of 644.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>with an initial Coulombic efficiency (CE) of 77.8%. The 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode exhibits excellent cycling stability and a capacity of 457.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> can be achieved beyond 150 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, much higher than 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode (363.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b). The phenomenon of the initial capacity decay and then rising has been also observed among other transition metal compounds. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 30 and 31">(30,31)</a> In the initial several cycles, because of the formation of SEI and the sluggish electrolyte infiltration into the active material, the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode delivers a much lower capacity. During the further cycling, the electrode realizes the enhanced electrochemical utilization, thus the capacity increases gradually. In addition, the continuous increase of capacity is also related to the expansion of the interlayer spacings of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> after long-term cycling. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31,32)</a></p><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/medium/nl3c04208_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Sodium storage performance of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>. (a) Discharged/charged profiles of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (b) Cycle performance and (c) rate performance of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub>, respectively. (d) The electrochemical performance comparison among 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> and other reported MoS<sub>2</sub>-based anodes. (e) Cycle performance at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (f) Charged/discharged curves of NVP/C||1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> full cells at 0.5 C. (g) Rate performance of full cells. (h) Cycling performance at 5 C of full cells.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> also achieves outstanding rate performance with capacity of 403.8 and 305.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.5 and 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>). Impressively, at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>, a high capacity of 266.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> can be achieved, which is much higher than that of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (196.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>). Among the reported MoS<sub>2</sub>-based anodes, the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits one of the best properties in SIBs (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22 ref25 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22 ref25 ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 22, 25 and 33 to 39">(22,25,33−39)</a> Moreover, the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode delivers good cycling reversibility (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>e). A high capacity of 358.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> is retained beyond 350 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p><p>The full cells (NVP/C||1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>) were assembled with 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> as the anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C (NVP/C) as the cathode. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a> shows the electrochemical performance of the NVP/C cathode. The NVP/C||1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> full cells deliver a discharged capacity of 100.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> and an average operating voltage of 3.0 V at 0.5 C (1 C = 117.6 mA g<sup>–1</sup>), and the calculated energy density is 300.3 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>f). The full cells show excellent rate performance (67.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 10  C) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>g). Moreover, the full cells also show excellent cycling performance, maintaining 80% capacity after 300 cycles at 5 C (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>h).</p><p>CV tests of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> half cells were conducted at various scan rates (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a). The shape of these CV profiles remains consistent, as the scan rate increases, a slight negative shift and positive shift of the cathodic peaks and anodic peaks are observed, respectively, delivering low polarization during the sodiation/desodiation process. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Equation S1</a> describes the relation between currents (<i>i</i>) and sweep rates (<i>v</i>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40 ref41 ref42" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref40 ref41 ref42" aria-label="reference 40 to 42">(40−42)</a> For the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode, the <i>b</i> values of peak O1, peak R1 and peak R2 are close to 1 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>), suggesting that the capacitive reaction dominates the leading role. Furthermore, the percentages of capacitive contribution at different scan rates are quantified (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Equation S2</a>). The results indicate that the capacitive contribution is gradually improved with the increasing of the scan rates. 93% capacitive contribution can be realized at 1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b). The high ratio of the capacitive contribution of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> leads to fast sodium storage kinetics, which endows  excellent rate capability.</p><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/medium/nl3c04208_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Dynamics and electrochemical reaction mechanisms of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> for sodium storage. (a) CV curves of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> at different scan rates. (b) The capacitive contribution ratios of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>, respectively. (c) GITT potential profiles of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>, respectively. (d) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients. (e) Nyquist curves of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrodes, respectively. (f) <i>Ex situ</i> Raman patterns of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode. (g) HRTEM image of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode at fully charged state (3.0 V). (h) <i>In situ</i> EIS curves of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> at different discharged/charged potentials during the first cycle. (i) Change of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode during the first cycle.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) curves of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> show similar tendencies (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c). The values of diffusion coefficient for Na<sup>+</sup> (<i>D</i><sub class="stack">Na</sub><sup class="stack">+</sup>) were calculated from <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Equation S3</a>. Notably,  1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits a higher <i>D</i><sub class="stack">Na</sub><sup class="stack">+</sup> than 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> during the sodiation/desodiation process, indicating much superior reaction kinetics (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>d). According to the electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) results (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>e), the calculated <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode is 5.4 Ω, much lower than 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode (12.2 Ω). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43 ref44" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref43 ref44" aria-label="reference 43 and 44">(43,44)</a> The larger interlayer spacing and enhanced electrical conductivity of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> introduced by Ni electronic donation can greatly improve the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics and the capacitive contribution, thus exhibiting vastly improved electrochemical properties.</p><p><i>Ex situ</i> Raman patterns were recorded to investigate the changes of the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode during the discharged/charged process (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>f). When discharged to 0.2 V, the peaks of the 1T (J<sub>1</sub>, J<sub>2</sub>, E<sub>1g</sub> and J<sub>3</sub>) and 2H phases (E<sub class="stack">2g</sub><sup class="stack">1</sup> and A<sub>1g</sub>) all disappear, indicating  breakage of the Mo–S bonds. However, at charged state (3.0 V), the peaks of the two phases reappear, demonstrating the reconstruction of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>. Moreover, the peaks of the 1T phase are still maintained after 50 cycles, indicating excellent stability of the 1T phase during the repeated sodiation/desodiation process (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>). Furthermore, TEM tests were carried out to characterize the structure change at discharged and charged states. In the fully discharged state (0.2 V) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9a</a>), the discharged products Na<sub>2</sub>S and V are generated. However, once the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode is charged to 3.0 V, the 2H and 1T phases of MoS<sub>2</sub> appear again (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9b</a>). Furthermore, The HRTEM image in the charged state (3.0 V) displays that the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode has significantly enlarged interlayer spacing (1.14 nm) compared with the original 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> nanoflowers (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>g). The EDS mappings display the homogeneous dispersion of Mo, S and Ni elements in the obtained sample (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10</a>). The above results confirm that 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> has a high electrochemical reversibility and stability during the electrochemical process.</p><p>Besides, the <i>in situ</i> EIS measurements during the first cycling were conducted (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>h). During the discharged process, with the intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup>, the value of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> decreases quickly and reaches 2.5 Ω at 1.2 V (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>i). Subsequently increases to 3.1 Ω at 0.7 V, which indicates the gradual formation of SEI. At the fully discharged state (0.2 V), the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value decreased to 2.2 Ω, which originates from the formation of metal Mo from the conversion reaction. the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value gradually increases during the later charged process. At the fully charged state (3.0 V), the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value reaches 4.2 Ω. In addition, the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode delivers a lower <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value (7.1 Ω) compared to the 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (18.6 Ω) after 50 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>). The above results indicate that the 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> electrode exhibits rapid reaction kinetics during the electrochemical reaction process.</p><p>The electron configuration modulation mechanism of MoS<sub>2</sub> by Ni electron injection and its enhanced electrochemical performance were further investigated by DFT calculations. Firstly, the possible existence sites of Ni in MoS<sub>2</sub> were studied. Through calculations, it was found that the intercalation of Ni into the MoS<sub>2</sub> interlayer will cause the <i>c</i>-axis of both 2H and 1T phases shrink and the interlayer spacings decrease (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12, 13</a>), which is inconsistent with the broadened layer spacing of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> in the TEM results (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>d). In addition, the charge density difference and Bader charge results show that the introduction of Ni into the 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> interlayer causes the electrons on Mo to decrease by 0.06 e<sup>–</sup> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S14</a>), which is contradictory to the electrons increase of Mo  at the XPS results (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>d). The above results rule out the possibility of Ni intercalation between the MoS<sub>2</sub> layers. Another possible site is that Ni located in the transition metal layers of MoS<sub>2</sub>. 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> is thermodynamically stable phase compared to the 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S15</a>) according to the energy variance between 1T and 2H phase (Δ<i>E</i> = <i>E</i><sub>1T</sub> – <i>E</i><sub>2H</sub> = 0.81 eV/per MoS<sub>2</sub> unit). It is worth noting that the energy difference decreases to 0.44 eV/per MoS<sub>2</sub> unit after the introduction of Ni into the transition metal layers (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S16</a>), indicating that the phase transition of MoS<sub>2</sub> becomes easier. The electron density difference of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a. The simulation results display that Ni can donate partial electrons to the Mo. Consequently, the electron configuration of Mo 4d orbitals will be rearranged and divided into d<sub><i>xy</i></sub>/d<sub><i>xz</i></sub>/d<sub><i>yz</i></sub> and d<sub><i>z</i><sup>2</sup></sub>/d<sub><i>x</i><sup>2</sup>–<i>y</i><sup>2</sup></sub> energy levels. The extra electrons will occupy the lower energy level d<sub><i>xy</i></sub>/d<sub><i>xz</i></sub>/d<sub><i>yz</i></sub> degenerate orbitals, making the structure of 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> more stable (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b). The Bader charge also shows  charge transfer (0.12 e<sup>–</sup>) from Ni to Mo after the introduction of Ni, which is consistent with the previous XPS results.</p><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/medium/nl3c04208_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) Charge density difference of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> (green represents charge accumulation and purple represents charge depletion). (b)  Mo 4d-orbitals of 2H and 1T phase MoS<sub>2</sub>, respectively. (c) The  adsorption energy of Na (the insets are corresponding adsorption structures). (d)  DOS patterns of 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>, respectively. (e)  The diffusion barriers of Na. (f)  Na migration path in 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/asset/images/large/nl3c04208_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p>The electrical conductivity and ion diffusion properties of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> were simulated. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S17</a> shows the optimized adsorption models of Na. The adsorption energy (Δ<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>) value of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> is −2.74 eV, much negative than 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (−1.06 eV) and 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> (−2.05 eV) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c). The total density of states (DOS) patterns (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d) show that the 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> delivers semiconducting property. Conversely, the electron density of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> near the Fermi level  increases, exhibiting metallic conductivity. Furthermore, the diffusion barrier of Na in 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> (0.09 eV) is lower than that in 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub> (0.73 eV) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>e). The corresponding migration path of Na is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>f. The proper introduction of Ni  can facilitate the electrical conductivity and boost the migration dynamics of Na<sup>+</sup>, thereby improving its sodium storage performance.</p><p class="last">In summary, a facile electron configuration modulation strategy is adopted to prepare stable 1T-MoS<sub>2</sub> assisted by Ni electron injection. The extra electrons donated by Ni in MoS<sub>2</sub> will cause the Mo 4d orbitals rearrangement, leading to the change of MoS<sub>2</sub> from 2H to 1T phase. DFT calculation results show that 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits high electrical conductivity and a much lower diffusion barrier of Na. Therefore,  1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> exhibits excellent electrochemical performance. It delivers high discharged capacity (644.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>), outstanding rate capability (266.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>) and long cycling life (358.7 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> maintained beyond 350 cycles at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>). Furthermore, the Na<sup>+</sup> full cells (1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> as anodes and NVP/C as cathodes) provide discharged capacity of 100.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with energy density of 300.3 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at 0.5  C. In addition, the full cells deliver excellent rate capability (67.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 10 C). Moreover, it also exhibits excellent cycling stability at 5  C with a high capacity retention of 80% beyond 300 cycles. This research paves the way for simple, scalable  and facile electron configuration modulation strategy to design high-performance electrode materials and facilitate the practical application for sodium ion storage.</p><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Experimental and calculation details, additional characterizations of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub>, additional electrochemical measurements and additional DFT computations (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf">nl3c04208_si_001.pdf (1.12 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interfacial engineering to achieve an energy density of over 200 Wh kg-1 in sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yuqi; Zhou, Quan; Weng, Suting; Ding, Feixiang; Qi, Xingguo; Lu, Jiaze; Li, Yu; Zhang, Xiao; Rong, Xiaohui; Lu, Yaxiang; Wang, Xuefeng; Xiao, Ruijuan; Li, Hong; Huang, Xuejie; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-based batteries have attracted wide interests in the academic and industrial fields.  However, their energy d. is still lower than that of Li-based batteries.  Here we report an initial anode-free Na battery with an energy d. of over 200 Wh kg-1, which is even higher than that of the com. LiFePO4||graphite battery.  Through introducing graphitic carbon coating on the Al current collector and boron-contg. electrolytes in the battery, we show that uniform nucleation and robust interphases enable reversible and crack-free Na deposition.  Benefitting from the synergetic effects derived from the built cooperative interfaces, the cycling lifetime of the Na battery without applying addnl. pressure reaches 260 cycles, which is the longest life for large-size cells with zero excess Na.  The insights gained from the Na plating/stripping behavior and interfacial chem. in this work pave the way for further development of Na batteries with even higher performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202218282"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, J.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Evolution of Stabilized 1T-MoS2 by Atomic-Interface Engineering of 2H-MoS2/Fe-Nx towards Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xia, Huicong; Zan, Lingxing; Yuan, Pengfei; Qu, Gan; Dong, Hongliang; Wei, Yifan; Yu, Yue; Wei, Zeyu; Yan, Wenfu; Hu, Jin-Song; Deng, Dehui; Zhang, Jia-Nan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">62</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">e202218282</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic conductive 1T phase molybdenum sulfide (MoS2) has been identified as promising anode for sodium ion (Na+) batteries, but its metastable feature makes it difficult to obtain and its restacking during the charge/discharge processing result in part capacity reversibility.  Herein, a synergetic effect of at.-interface engineering is employed for constructing 2H-MoS2 layers assembled on single atomically dispersed Fe-N-C (SA Fe-N-C) anode material that boosts its reversible capacity.  The work-function-driven-electron transfer occurs from SA Fe-N-C to 2H-MoS2 via the Fe-S bonds, which enhances the adsorption of Na+ by 2H-MoS2, and lays the foundation for the sodiation process.  A phase transfer from 2H to 1T/2H MoS2 with the ferromagnetic spin-polarization of SA Fe-N-C occurs during the sodiation/desodiation process, which significantly enhances the Na+ storage kinetics, and thus the 1T/2H MoS2/SA Fe-N-C display a high electronic cond. and a fast Na+ diffusion rate.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202202673"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Integrating Bi@C Nanospheres in Porous Hard Carbon Frameworks for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2202673</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.202202673</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D34%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DY.%2BLiang%26author%3DN.%2BSong%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BFeng%26author%3DB.%2BXi%26author%3DS.%2BXiong%26title%3DIntegrating%2BBi%2540C%2BNanospheres%2Bin%2BPorous%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BFrameworks%2Bfor%2BUltrafast%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202202673&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202202673&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Integrating Bi@C Nanospheres in Porous Hard Carbon Frameworks for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Yazhan; Song, Ning; Zhang, Zhengchunyu; Chen, Weihua; Feng, Jinkui; Xi, Baojuan; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">28</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2202673</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have emerged as an alternative technol. because of their merits in abundance and cost.  Realizing their real applications, however, remains a formidable challenge.  One is that among the limitations of anode materials, the alloy-type candidates tolerate fast capacity fading during cycling.  Here, a 3D framework superstructure assembled with carbon nanobelt arrays decorated with a metallic bismuth (Bi) nanospheres coated carbon layer by thermolysis of Bi-based metal-org. framework nanorods is synthesized as an anode material for SIBs.  Due to the unique structural superiority, the anode design promotes excellent sodium-storage performance in terms of high capacity, excellent cycling stability, and ultrahigh rate capability up to 80 A g-1 with a capacity of 308.8 mAh g-1.  The unprecedented sodium-storage ability is not only attributed to the unique hybrid architecture, but also to the prodn. of a homogeneous and thin solid electrolyte interface layer and the formation of uniform porous nanostructures during cycling in the ether-based electrolyte.  Importantly, deeper understanding of the underlying cause of the performance improvement is illuminated, which is vital to provide the theor. basis for application of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.03.036"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Novel Layer-by-Layer Stacked VS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets with Intercalation Pseudocapacitance for High-Rate Sodium Ion Charge Storage</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>35</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">396</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">404</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel layer-by-layer stacked VS2 nanosheets with intercalation pseudocapacitance for high-rate sodium ion charge storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ruimin; Wei, Qiulong; Sheng, Jinzhi; Shi, Changwei; An, Qinyou; Liu, Sijie; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">396-404</span>CODEN:
