        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a promising candidate for large scale energy storage systems due to their low cost and reasonable performance.  However, developing desirable anode materials with high capacity, excellent cycling stability and high rate capability remains great challenges.  Herein, novel layer-by-layer VS2 stacked nanosheets (VS2-SNSs) are synthesized using a facile one-step polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP) assisted assembly method.  With a highly stable orderly stacked layer structure, the VS2 delivers excellent electrochem. performance in SIBs.  A reversible discharge capacity of 250 mA h g-1 is obtained at 0.2 A g-1.  A high specific capacity of 150 mA h g-1 even at 20 A g-1 is reached (discharged/charged in 27 s).  Furthermore, the VS2-SNSs deliver long cycling life with almost no capacity fading even after 600 cycles at 5 A g-1.  In-situ XRD and ex-situ TEM characterization reveal that VS2 undertakes a reversible intercalation reaction mechanism.  A detailed electrochem. kinetic anal. reveals that the sodium ion charge storage depends on intercalation pseudocapacitive behavior with a high capacitive contribution up to 69% for the total capacity at 1 mV s-1.  The impressive electrochem. performance reveals that the VS2 has great potential for the next generation large scale energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201701744"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mesoporous NiS<sub>2</sub> Nanospheres Anode with Pseudocapacitance for High-Rate and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1701744</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Inspired by nature: Self-fractal cobalt sulfate composite electrode for sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Man; Liu, Xiaoxu; Gu, Jiangdong; Wang, Hui; Liu, Hui; Shen, Zexiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Chemical Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Generally, the metal sulfide itself has poor cond., and the vol. expansion occurs when it is converted with sodium, which will destroy the integrity of the electrode structure, resulting in poor cycle performance and rate performance.  To solve the problems of low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) and vol. expansion of metal compds. used as anodes in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Inspired by nature, the CoSO4/hard carbon/graphene (CHG) fractal structure electrode was designed.  Self-fractal structures with electron/ion transport channels and high strain tolerance proved to be an effective strategy to overcome these challenges.  The fractal dimension (D) is measured by synchronous Small Angle X-ray scattering, and the D remains stable during charging and discharging.  The fractal CHG also showed excellent electrochem. performance, esp. 97.4% ICE.  Theor. calcn. shows that self-fractal CHG can promote the formation of a thin solid electrolyte interface (SEI).  Synchrotron radiation absorption spectrum proved the reaction mechanism of CHG.  This study not only proves that cobalt sulfate is a feasible strategy for developing high-performance SIBs anodes but also provides an advanced method for measuring the fractal dimension of energy storage electrode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref8" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202212785"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of VS<sub>2</sub>/VO<sub><i>x</i></sub> Heterostructure Via Hydrolysis-Oxidation Coupling Reaction with Superior Sodium Storage Properties</span>. <i>Adv. Herein, based on the spontaneous hydrolysis-oxidn. coupling reaction of transition metal sulfides in aq. media, a VOx layer is induced and formed on the surface of VS2, realizing tight combination of VS2 and VOx at the nanoscale and constructing homologous VS2/VOx heterostructure.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering strategies of metal-organic frameworks toward advanced batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ruimin; Dou, Mingyue; Chen, Ziliang; Wang, Ruirui; Zheng, Xiangyi; Zhang, Yuxiang; Zhou, Chenggang; Menezes, Prashanth W.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Battery Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) integrate several advantages such as adjustable pore sizes, large sp. surface areas, controllable geometrical morphol., and feasible surface modification.  Benefiting from these appealing merits, MOFs have recently been extensively explored in the field of advanced secondary batteries.  However, a systematic summarization of the specific functional units that these materials can act as in batteries as well as their related design strategies to underline their functions has not been perceived to date.  Motivated by this point, this review dedicates to the elucidation of diverse functions of MOFs for batteries, which involve the electrodes, separators, interface modifiers, and electrolytes.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-coated MoS1.5Te0.5 nanocables for efficient sodium-ion storage in non-aqueous dual-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yangjie; Hu, Xiang; Li, Junwei; Zhong, Guobao; Yuan, Jun; Zhan, Hongbing; Tang, Yongbing; Wen, Zhenhai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-based dual-ion batteries have received increased attention owing to their appealing cell voltage (i.e., &gt;3 V) and cost-effective features.  However, the development of high-performance anode materials is one of the key elements for exploiting this electrochem. energy storage system at practical levels.  Here, we report a source-template synthetic strategy for fabricating a variety of nanowire-in-nanotube MSxTey@C (M = Mo, W, Re) structures with an in situ-grown carbon film coating, termed as nanocables.  Among the various materials prepd., the MoS1.5Te0.5@C nanocables are investigated as neg. electrode active material in combination with expanded graphite at the pos. electrode and NaPF6-based non-aq. electrolyte solns. for dual-ion storage in coin cell configuration.  As a result, the dual-ion lab-scale cells demonstrate a prolonged cycling lifespan with 97% capacity retention over 1500 cycles and a reversible capacity of about 101 mAh g-1 at specific capacities (based on the mass of the anode) of 1.0 A g-1 and 5.0 A g-1, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref12" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202002600"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Approaching the Theoretical Sodium Storage Capacity and Ultrahigh Rate of Layer-Expanded MoS<sub>2</sub> by Interfacial Engineering on N-Doped Graphene</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Approaching the Theoretical Sodium Storage Capacity and Ultrahigh Rate of Layer-Expanded MoS2 by Interfacial Engineering on N-Doped Graphene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Shichuan; Zhang, Su; Liu, Zheng; Feng, Jing; Jiang, Zimu; Shi, Mengjiao; Chen, Lan; Wei, Tong; Fan, Zhuangjun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide holds great potential for sodium storage due to its high theor. capacity of 670 mAh g-1.  However, its theor. capacity is hardly realized because of low cond., sluggish electrochem. kinetics, and unsatisfied structural stability.  Herein, a polyaniline-mediated interfacial engineering strategy for the growth of interlayer-expanded molybdenum disulfide nanoflowers on nitrogen-doped graphene "land" (E-MoS2/NG) using Mo7O246- anions adsorbed on pos. charged polyaniline as the "seeds" is reported.  The strong interfacial interaction between molybdenum disulfide and graphene through Mo-N bonds as well as ultrathin interlayer-expanded molybdenum disulfide can significantly improve the electrochem. kinetics and structural stability.  As a result, E-MoS2/NG with a high molybdenum disulfide content of 90 wt% shows a high capacity (620 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), an ultrahigh rate capability (201 mAh g-1 at 50 A g-1), and outstanding cycle performance (390 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1).  Importantly, MoS2 in the composite approaches its theor. capacity of 670 mAh g-1.  Furthermore, the assembled E-MoS2/NG//activated carbon sodium ion capacitor delivers high energy densities of 150 and 82 Wh kg-1 at 35 and 14 421 W kg-1, resp., and a capacity retention of 78.1% after 1500 cycles at 10 A g-1, demonstrating great potential for practical application.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202000952"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Octahedra Constructed by Cu<sub>2</sub>S/MoS<sub>2</sub>⊂Carbon Framework with Enhanced Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2000952</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Octahedra Constructed by Cu2S/MoS2 Carbon Framework with Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Nianxiang; Xi, Baojuan; Huang, Man; Ma, Xiaojian; Li, Haibo; Feng, Jinkui; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal sulfides have aroused considerable attention for efficient sodium storage because of their high capacity and decent redox reversibility.  However, the poor rate capability and fast capacity decay greatly hinder their practical application in sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, a self-template-based strategy is designed to controllably synthesize hierarchical microoctahedra assembled with Cu2S/MoS2 heterojunction nanosheets in the porous carbon framework (Cu2S/MoS2 PCF) via a facile copptn. method coupled with vulcanization treatment.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Aging mechanism of MoS2 nanosheets confined in N-doped mesoporous carbon spheres for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Mingzhen; Qiu, Yongting; Yan, Guanfusheng; Wang, Jinming; Zhan, Da; Liu, Xiang; Gao, Jingchang; Lai, Linfei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped hollow carbon nanospheres (NHCS) with mesoporous carbon shells is selected as nanoreactors and encapsulated with few-layered MoS2 nanosheets to monitor its electrochem. properties and structural conversion in long-term cycling.  Mesoporous walls of NHCS can facilitate electrolyte penetration and provide conductive shells for superior mass diffusion and charge transfer.  When serving as SIB anodes, MoS2@NHCS has a capacity value of 371 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 94.9% after 100 cycles which is higher than powder form MoS2 and is among the highest values of earlier reported MoS2 electrodes.  The origin of gradual capacity decay of MoS2@NHCS anodes in-between 50 to 150 cycles has been investigated.  Transmission electron microscopy and ex-situ X-ray diffraction have shown significant morphol. change of space-confined MoS2 and the prodn. of MoO3 together with oxygen-deficient MoOx after continuous charge/discharge test.  After long-term cycle test of MoS2@NHCS, the ratios of Mo6+ and Mo5+ increased significantly with the decreasing of Mo4+ ratio, while the sulfur from MoS2 transformed from S2- to SO2-4.  This work highlight the phase transformation and compn. change of MoS2 for MoS2-based anode in long-duration charge/discharge tests.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Development of Metallic (1T) Phase of Molybdenum Disulfide for Energy Conversion and Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrocatalysts based on MoS2 and WS2 for hydrogen evolution reaction: An overview</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Van Nguyen, Tuan; Tekalgne, Mahider; Nguyen, Thang Phan; Van Le, Quyet; Ahn, Sang Hyun; Kim, Soo Young</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Battery Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20220057</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">BEANAC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2768-1696</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Recently, hydrogen energy has been significantly investigated by numerous technologies.  To date, noble platinum group metals have often been employed to fabricate working electrodes for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  Therefore, the demand of highly active HER catalysts based on effective and lower-cost materials is becoming more and more crit.  Transition metal dichalcogenide (TMD) materials could be one of the most suitable materials for these requirements because they possess numerous unique mech., electronic, and chem. characteristics that are greatly beneficial for HER processes.  Among many TMD materials, tungsten disulfide (WS2) and molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) are the most well-known TMD materials which have been intensively studied for different applications, including HER, batteries, and super capacitors.  In this review, we tried to cover the HER mechanism of catalysts and their parameters.  Besides that, the structures, properties, prepn., and HER performance of catalyst materials based on WS2 and MoS2 are comprehensively discussed.  After that, the challenges and future trends of catalysts based on WS2 and MoS2 for HER are also considered.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201703754"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kochat, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Apte, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hachtel, J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electron-Injection-Engineering Induced Phase Transition toward Stabilized 1T-MoS2 with Extraordinary Sodium Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Li, Xiaolong; Huang, Dan; Luan, Jinyi; Liu, Sailin; Pang, Wei Kong; Sun, Dan; Tang, Yougen; Zhou, Wenzheng; He, Lirong; Zhang, Chuhong; Wang, Haiyan; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8896-8906</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phase transition engineering, with the ability to alter the electronic structure and physicochem. properties of materials, has been widely used to achieve the thermodynamically unstable metallic phase MoS2 (1T-MoS2), although the complex operating conditions and low yield of previous strategies make the large-scale fabrication of 1T-MoS2 a big challenge.  Herein, we report a facile electron injection strategy for phase transition engineering and fabricate a composite of conductive TiO chem. bonded to 1T-MoS2 nanoflowers (TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs) on a large scale.  The underlying mechanism anal. reveals that electron-injection-engineering triggers a reorganization of the Mo 4d orbitals and results in a 100% phase transition of MoS2 from 2H to 1T.  In the TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs composite, the 1T-MoS2 demonstrates a higher electronic cond., a lower Na+ diffusion barrier, and a more restricted S release than 2H-MoS2.  In addn., conductive TiO bonding successfully resolves the stability challenge of the 1T phase.  These merits endow TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs electrodes with an excellent rate capability (650/288 mAh g-1 at 50/20 000 mA g-1, resp.) and an outstanding cyclability (501 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 700 cycles) in sodium ion batteries.  Such an improvement signifies that this facile and scalable phase-transition engineering combined with a deep mechanism anal. offers an important ref. for designing advanced materials for various applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202303464"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electron Modulated and Phosphate Radical Stabilized 1T-Rich MoS<sub>2</sub> for Ultra-Fast-Charged Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Diffusion mechanism and electrochemical investigation of 1T phase Al-MoS2@rGO nano-composite as a high-performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Singh, Manish Kr.; Pati, Jayashree; Seth, Deepak; Prasad, Jagdees; Agarwal, Manish; Haider, M. Ali; Chang, Jeng-Kuei; Dhaka, Rajendra S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">454</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. investigation of 5% Al doped MoS2@rGO composite as a high-performance anode for sodium (Na)-ion batteries.  The x-ray diffraction (XRD), Raman spectroscopy and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy characterizations reveal that the Al doping increase the interlayer spacing of (002) plane of MoS2 nanosheets and form a stable 1T phase.  The galvanostatic charge-discharge measurements show the specific capacity stable around 450, 400, 350, 300 and 200 mAhg-1 at current densities of 0.05, 0.1, 0.3, 0.5 and 1 Ag-1, resp.  Also, we observe the capacity retentions of 86% and 66% at 0.1 and 0.3 Ag-1, resp., over 200 cycles with a consistent Coulombic efficiency of nearly 100%.  The cyclic voltammetry, galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy are used to find the kinetic behavior and the obtained value of diffusion coeff. falls in the range of 10-10 to 10-12 cm2s-1.  Intriguingly, the in-situ EIS also explains the electrochem. kinetics of the electrode at different charge-discharge states with the variation of charge transfer resistance.  Moreover, the post cycling investigation using ex-situ XRD and photoemission spectroscopy indicate the coexistence of 1T/2H phase and field-emission SEM confirm the stable morphol. after 500 cycles.  Also, the Na-ion transport properties are calcd. for 1T Al-MoS2@rGO interface and Al-MoS2-MoS2 interlayer host structure by theor. calcns. using d. functional theory.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.2c03623"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lian, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jing, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wong, C.                 10.1021/acsnano.2c03623</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D12425-12436%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DJ.%2BSun%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DG.%2BLian%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BJing%26author%3DM.%2BZhao%26author%3DD.%2BCui%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BYu%26author%3DC.%2BP.%2BWong%26title%3DElectron-Injection%2Band%2BAtomic-Interface%2BEngineering%2Btoward%2BStabilized%2BDefected%2B1T-Rich%2BMoS2%2Bas%2BHigh%2BRate%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.2c03623&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c03623&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electron-Injection and Atomic-Interface Engineering toward Stabilized Defected 1T-Rich MoS2 as High Rate Anode for Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Junwei; Zhang, Zhihua; Lian, Gang; Li, Yangyang; Jing, Laiying; Zhao, Mingwen; Cui, Deliang; Wang, Qilong; Yu, Haohai; Wong, Ching-Ping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12425-12436</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">1T-phase MoS2 is a promising electrode material for electrochem. energy storage due to its metallic cond., abundant active sites, and high theor. capacity.  However, because of the habitual conversion of metastable 1T to stable 2H phase via restacking, the poor rate capacity and cycling stability at high current densities hamper their applications.  Herein, a synergetic effect of electron-injection engineering and at.-interface engineering is employed for the formation and stabilization of defected 1T-rich MoS2 nanoflowers.  The 1T-rich MoS2 and carbon monolayers are alternately intercalated with each other in the nanohybrids.  The metallic 1T-phase MoS2 and conductive carbon monolayers are favorable for charge transport.  The expanded interlayer spacing ensures fast electrolyte diffusion and the decrease of the ion diffusion barrier.  The obtained defected 1T-rich MoS2/m-C nanoflowers exhibit high Na-storage capacity (557 mAh g-1 after 80 cycles at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate capacity (411 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and long-term cycling performance (364 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at 2 A g-1).  Furthermore, a Na-ion full cell composed of the 1T-rich MoS2/m-C anode and Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode maintains excellent cycling stability at 0.5 A g-1 during 400 cycles.  Theor. calcns. are also performed to evaluate the phase stability, electronic cond., and Na+ diffusion behavior of 1T-rich MoS2/m-C.  The energy storage performance demonstrates its excellent application prospects.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.04.063"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abd Ei-Hady, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshitari, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saad Al-Bogami, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">1T MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets with Extraordinary Sodium Storage Properties Via Thermal-Driven Ion Intercalation Assisted Exfoliation of Bulky MoS<sub>2</sub></span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>61</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">361</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">369</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">1T MoS2 nanosheets with extraordinary sodium storage properties via thermal-driven ion intercalation assisted exfoliation of bulky MoS2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Dan; Huang, Dan; Wang, Haiyan; Xu, Gui-Liang; Zhang, Xiaoyi; Zhang, Rui; Tang, Yougen; Abd Ei-Hady, Deia; Alshitari, Wael; Saad Al-Bogami, Abdullah; Amine, Khalil; Shao, Minhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic phase (1T) MoS2 has attracted enormous attention as an appealing energy storage material for batteries, supercapacitors, and catalysts.  However, a facile fabrication method is lacking and the intensive understanding of its sodium storage mechanism is absent.  Herein, ultrathin 1T MoS2 nanosheets (1-2 layers) are directly fabricated via and are investigated as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  Interestingly, the as-prepd. 1T MoS2 nanosheets demonstrate a high reversible capacity of 450 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and outstanding cycling stability with a high capacity retention ratio of 94% after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1, which is far superior to that of the 2H phase counterpart.  D. function theory (DFT) calcns. show that, in addn. to significantly enhanced electronic cond., 1T MoS2 also possesses much more sodium philicity and faster Na atom mobility in comparison with the 2H phase.  More importantly, as revealed by ex-situ Raman, in-situ X-ray diffraction, and DFT calcns., the 1T MoS2 is more capable of suppressing the dissoln. of S species from the material structure compared with the 2H phase, leading to excellent cycling stability.  The facile and easily scalable method as well as the deep mechanism anal. will provide a very important ref. for the development of high-performance MoS2 anodes and other SIB electrode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA06905K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, W.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, X.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, C.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tu, J.-P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hollow Metallic 1T MoS<sub>2</sub> Arrays Grown on Carbon Cloth: A Freestanding Electrode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hollow metallic 1T MoS2 arrays grown on carbon cloth: a freestanding electrode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Wang-jia; Wang, Xiu-li; Xie, Dong; Xia, Xin-hui; Gu, Chang-dong; Tu, Jiang-ping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-Semiconductor Phase Twinned Hierarchical MoS2 Nanowires with Expanded Interlayers for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Ultralong Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Wei; Wu, Fangfang; Shi, Nianxiang; Zhou, Han; Chi, Qianqian; Chen, Weihua; Du, Shiyu; Gao, Peng; Li, Haibo; Xiong, Shenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered a prospective candidate for large-scale energy storage due to the merits of abundant sodium resources and low cost.  However, a lack of suitable advanced anode materials has hindered further applications.  Herein, metal-semiconductor mixed phase twinned hierarchical (MPTH) MoS2 nanowires with an expanded interlayer (9.63 Å) are engineered and prepd. using MoO3 nanobelts as a self-sacrificed template in the presence of a trace amt. of (NH4)6Mo7O24·4H2O as initiator. Benefiting from the structural merits, the MPTH MoS2 electrode delivers high reversible capacities of 200 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 for 200 cycles and 154 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 for 2450 cycles in the voltage range of 0.4-3.0 V.  Strikingly, the electrode maintains 6500 cycles at a c.d. of 2 A g-1, corresponding to a capacity retention of 82.8% of the 2nd cycle, overwhelming the all reported MoS2 cycling results.  This study provides an alternative strategy to boost SIB cycling performance in terms of reversible capacity by virtue of interlayer expansion and structure stability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA11913B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ihsan-Ul-Haq, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mubarak, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Quattrocchi, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ciucci, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dual-Phase MoS<sub>2</sub> as a High-Performance Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Metal-Organic Frameworks Derived 1T-MoS2 with Expanded Layer Spacing for Enhanced Electrocatalytic Hydrogen Evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Hang; Xu, Hualan; Wang, Lei; Ouyang, Chuying; Liang, Haiwei; Zhong, Shengliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

Here, a one-step solvothermal route is developed to prep. 1T-MoS2 with expanded layer spacing through the derivatization of a Mo-based org. framework (Mo-MOFs).  Benefiting from N,N-dimethylformamide oxide as external stress, the interplanar spacing of (002) of the MoS2 catalyst is extended to 10.87 S, which represents the largest one for the 1T-MoS2 catalyst prepd. by the bottom-up approach.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Anchoring Anion-Rich and Multi-Cavity NiS2 Nanoparticles on NCNTs for Advanced Magnesium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ye, Zisen; Li, Ping; Wei, Wutao; Huang, Chao; Mi, Liwei; Zhang, Jinglai; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Magnesium (Mg)-ion batteries with low cost and good safety characteristics has attracted a great deal of attention recently.  However, the high polarity and the slow diffusion of Mg2+ in the cathode material limit the development of practical Mg cathode materials.  In this paper, an anion-rich electrode material, NiS2, and its composite with Ni-based carbon nanotubes (NiS2/NCNTs) are explored as the cathode materials for Mg-ion batteries.  These NiS2/NCNTs with excellent Mg2+ storage property is synthesized by a simple in situ growth of NiS2 nanoparticles on NCNTs.  NiS2 with both a large regular cavity structure and abundant sulfur-sulfur (SS) bonds with high electronegativity can provide a large no. of active sites and unobstructed transport paths for the insertion-disinsertion of Mg2+.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the wide range and low cost of sodium resources, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have received extensive attention and research.  Metal sulfides with high theor. capacity are used as promising anode materials for SIBs.  This paper presents the electrochem. performance of the binder-free NiS2 nanosheet arrays grown on stainless steel (SS) substrate (NiS2/SS) using an in situ growth and sulfidation strategy as anode for sodium ion batteries.  Owing to the close connection between the NiS2 nanosheet arrays and the SS current collector, the NiS2/SS anode demonstrates high rate capability with a reversible capacity of 492.5 mAh·g-1 at 5.0C rate.  Such rate capability is superior to that of NiS2 nanoparticles (NiS2/CMC: 41.7 mAh·g-1 at 5.0C, NiS2/PVDF: 7.3 mAh·g-1 at 5.0C) and other Ni sulfides (100-450 mAh·g-1 at 5.0C) reported.  Furthermore, the initial reversible specific capacity and Coulombic efficiency of NiS2/SS are 786.5 mAh·g-1 and 81%, resp., demonstrating a better sodium storage ability than those of most NiS2 anodes reported for SIBs. Herein, sandwich structure hierarchical nanofibers composed of hollow carbon fibers as the substrate, and MoS2 as the interlayer with Co and/or ZnS nanoparticles anchoring in carbon skeletons as the outer shell (carbon nanofiber/MoS2/Co-ZnS⊂NC) are prepd. via a multistep reaction strategy. A discharge capacity of 182.5 mAh g-1 is retained even after 10 000 cycles at 10.0 A g-1 as well as a high rate capacity of 202.0 mAh g-1 up to 30 A g-1.  The optimal at. ratio of Co element is further verified by the kinetic anal.  The full-cells assembled with Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode provide a high capacity of 179.2 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 for 500 cycles.  Combining in situ and ex situ characterizations and theor. calcns., possible sodium storage mechanisms and the origin of superior electrochem. properties are revealed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202000741"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Heterostructure SnSe<sub>2</sub>/ZnSe@PDA Nanobox for Stable and Highly Efficient Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/aenm.202000741</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DP.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BHan%26author%3DK.%2BZhu%26author%3DZ.%2BDong%26author%3DL.%2BJiao%26title%3DHeterostructure%2BSnSe2%252FZnSe%2540PDA%2BNanobox%2Bfor%2BStable%2Band%2BHighly%2BEfficient%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202000741&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.3c04208&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202000741&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heterostructure SnSe2/ZnSe@PDA Nanobox for Stable and Highly Efficient Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Pei; Han, Jun; Zhu, Kunjie; Dong, Zihao; Jiao, Lifang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000741</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rationally designed electrode materials with high capacity, long cycle life, and low cost are indispensable for sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, a hierarchical nanobox consisting of a heterojunction bimetallic selenide yolk and polydopamine shell (denoted as SnSe2/ZnSe@PDA) is engineered and fabricated successfully.  Owing to the charge redistribution and lattice distortion at the hetero-phase boundaries, Na+ ions can be easily adsorbed and transferred swiftly, facilitating the reaction kinetics and promoting cycling behavior.  By means of the hollow structure and elastic polymer shell, this approach can synergistically alleviate vol. fluctuation and the aggregation of active nanomaterials during cycling.  This material delivers a high reversible capacity of 616 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 over 1000 long-term cycles, and superior rate capability, which provides more possibilities for the practical applications of energy storage in the future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b00383"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical MoS<sub>2</sub> Hollow Architectures with Abundant Mo Vacancies for Efficient Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5533</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5540</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical MoS2 Hollow Architectures with Abundant Mo Vacancies for Efficient Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yang; Zhang, Rupeng; Zhou, Wei; Wu, Xin; Zhang, Huabin; Zhang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Achieving a mol. level understanding of surface performance of nanomaterials by modulating the electronic structure is important but challenging.  Here, the authors have developed a hollow microcube framework constructed by Mo-defect-rich ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets (HMF-MoS2) through a zeolite-like-framework-engaged strategy.  The hollow structured HMF-MoS2 delivers an impressive specific capacity (384.3 mA-h/g after 100 cycles at 100 mA/g) and cycle stability (267 mA-h/g after 125 cycles at 1 A/g) for sodium storage.  As evidenced by expts. and d. functional theory calcns., abundant Mo vacancies in MoS2 can greatly accelerate the charge transfer and enhance the interaction between MoS2 and sodium, resulting in the promotion of sodium storage.  Kinetic anal. result reveals that the ultrafast sodium ion storage of HMF-MoS2 could be assocd. with the significant contribution of capacitive energy storage.  This work highlights the detailed mol. level understanding of chem. reaction on MoS2 surface by defect and morphol. engineering, which can be applied to other metal sulfides for energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.03.060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Z.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, M.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sang, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, H.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Superelastic 3D Few-Layer MoS<sub>2</sub>/Carbon Framework Heterogeneous Electrodes for Highly Reversible Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>48</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">526</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">535</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superelastic 3D few-layer MoS2/carbon framework heterogeneous electrodes for highly reversible sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Zhi-Hao; Hu, Xu-Dong; Wang, Hongqiang; Ye, Meng-Yang; Sang, Zhi-Yuan; Ji, Hui-Ming; Li, Xiao-Lei; Dai, Yejing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">526-535</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rational design of electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries with high flexibility is still challenging.  Here, superelastic 3D few-layer MoS2/carbon framework heterogeneous electrodes (abbreviated as, MoS2@CF) are fabricated by a simple vacuum infiltration and heating process.  The interconnected ultrathin MoS2 network filled with carbon framework forms a 3D heterogeneous network with hierarchical pore structure.  The unique structure of the electrodes results in excellent mech. and electrochem. performances.  The MoS2@CF electrodes exhibit superior elasticity and recoverability.  After 180° bending repeatedly, the electrodes still can recover their initial sizes.  Moreover, the electrodes show outstanding cycling stabilities with high reversible capacities reaching up 240 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 A g-1 (capacity retention of ∼ 99%).  Full-cells assembled with MoS2@CF anodes and Na3V2(PO4)3 cathodes show high reversible capacity (∼ 252 mA h g-1 at 0.5 A g-1).  Overall, the superior mech. properties and high electrochem. performances indicate the promising potential of MoS2@CF electrodes in large-scale flexible sodium-ion storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.02.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jia, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tiep, N.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Few-atomic-layered hollow nanospheres constructed from alternate intercalation of carbon and MoS2 monolayers for sodium and lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Laiying; Lian, Gang; Niu, Feier; Yang, Jian; Wang, Qilong; Cui, Deliang; Wong, Ching-Ping; Liu, Xizheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">546-555</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite high theor. specific capacity and uniform interlayer channel for accommodation of ions, poor cycling stability and rate capacity have been identified as crit. roadblocks to further development of MoS2-based lithium ion batteries (LIBs) or sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  In this study, few-at.-layered MoS2 hollow nanospheres with expanded interlayer spacing, due to alternate intercalation of N-doped monolayer carbon (m-C) between the adjacent MoS2 monolayers, have been designed and synthesized via an annealing-followed soft-template approach.  As an anode of SIBs, the ultrathin-layered m-C/MoS2 superstructures electrode can deliver a reversible discharge capacity of 401 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 150 cycles.  It can maintain 262 mA h g-1 at 2000 mA g-1 after 600 cycles with a capacity retention of 105% in comparison with that of the 2nd cycle.  For LIBs, the hollow nanospheres can also deliver a reversible discharge capacity of 1025 mA h g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 80 cycles.  The excellent electrochem. performance can be attributed to the synergy effect of expanded interlayer spacing (improving ion diffusion mobility), ultrathin feature (shortening ion diffusion paths) and alternate intercalation of monolayer carbon (improving the elec. cond. and maintaining the structural integrity), which ensures new opportunities for designing advanced two-dimensional hosts for energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201800658"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controllable Design of MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets Anchored on Nitrogen-Doped Graphene: Toward Fast Sodium Storage by Tunable Pseudocapacitance</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid materials, integrating the merits of individual components, are ideal structures for efficient sodium storage.  However, the construction of hybrid structures with decent phys./electrochem. properties is still challenging.  Now, the elaborate design and synthesis of hierarchical nanoboxes composed of three-layered Cu2S@carbon@MoS2 as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries is reported.  Through a facile multistep template-engaged strategy, ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets are grown on nitrogen-doped carbon-coated Cu2S nanoboxes to realize the Cu2S@carbon@MoS2 configuration.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2), due to its high theor. specific capacity (670 mA h g-1), has evoked considerable investigation interest in the area of Na+ storage.  Nonetheless, the irreversible conversion of the original material MoS2 into Mo/Na2S during sodium insertion incurs rapid capacity degrdn.  Herein, to avoid this severe irreversibility, NayMoS2 is employed to replace the above irreversible products to facilitate subsequent sodium extn., achieving reversible transformation of the raw material.  In order to accomplish this goal, tremella-like hollow MoS2(1-x)Se2x-C (x = 0, 0.1, 0.25, 0.5) spheres are elaborately prepd. and then act as an appropriate anode material exhibiting good sodium storage capacity.  It is proved that doping with Se and regulating the cut-off voltage improve the layer spacing and bond strength, so that the Mo-S bond is maintained without irreversible change during the sodium storage process.  This work delivers a practical strategy to modify the energy storage ability via reversible transformation of the original material and proposes an appropriate Se doping amt., demonstrating effective measures for constructing a relevant advanced anode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202208291"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solvent Induced Activation Reaction of MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets within Nitrogen/Sulfur-Codoped Carbon Network Boosting Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2208291</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solvent Induced Activation Reaction of MoS2 Nanosheets within Nitrogen/Sulfur-Codoped Carbon Network Boosting Sodium Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Guangsheng; Li, Lixin; Zhu, Kai; Yan, Jun; Wang, Guiling; Cao, Dianxue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2, as a classical 2D material, becomes a capable anode candidate for sodium-ion batteries.  However, MoS2 presents a disparate electrochem. performance in the ether-based and ester-based electrolyte with unclear mechanism.  Herein, tiny MoS2 nanosheets embedded in nitrogen/sulfur-codoped carbon (MoS2@NSC) networks are designed and fabricated through an uncomplicated solvothermal method.  Thanks to the ether-based electrolyte, the MoS2@NSC shows a unique capacity growth in the original stage of cycling.  But in the ester-based electrolyte, MoS2@NSC shows a usual capacity decay.  The increasing capacity puts down to the gradual transformation from MoS2 to MoS3 with the structure reconstruction.  Based on the above mechanism, MoS2@NSC demonstrates an excellent recyclability and the specific capacity keeps around 286 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 5000 cycles with an ultralow capacity fading rate of only 0.0034% per cycle.  In addn., a MoS2@NSC Na3V2(PO4)3 full cell with ether-based electrolyte is assembled and demonstrates a capacity of 71 mAh g-1, suggesting the potential application of MoS2@NSC.  Here the electrochem. conversion mechanism of MoS2 is revealed in the ether-based electrolyte and significance of the electrolyte design on the promoting Na ion storage behavior is highlighted.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/bte2.20230001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanoemulsion-Directed Assembly of Hierarchical ZnS@C Nanospheres with Penetrating Pores for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Battery Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">20230001</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoemulsion-directed assembly of hierarchical ZnS@C nanospheres with penetrating pores for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Xiaowei; Zhuo, Sifei; Tian, Lidong; Qiao, Mingtao; Lei, Xingfeng; Zhang, Hepeng; Zhang, Qiuyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Battery Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To follow up on the performance of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), transition metal sulfides (TMSs) have been developed as promising carbon alternatives for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Although attractive, it is still a great challenge to fulfill their capacity utilization with high cycling performance.  Herein, a nanoemulsion-directed method has been developed to control the spherical arrangement of ZnS-C units with both penetrating macropores from the center to the surface and inner mesopores distributed among the bulks.  With respect to ion diffusion, the penetrating macropores could serve as the built-in ion-buffer reservoirs to keep a steady flow of electrolyte, while the inner mesopores facilitate the ion diffusion across the whole bulks.  In terms of stability, the radical porous structure could work as self-supported vertical bones to accommodate the vol. change from both lateral and vertical sides.  Besides, the localized carbon distributed among the ZnS nanoparticles not only acts as binding agents to join the numerous ZnS nanoparticles but also endows the radical bones with effective electron transmission capability.  As a proof of concept, such hydrangea-like ZnS-C nanospheres deliver sodium storage performance with high-rate and long-cycling capability.  This nanoemulsion-directed approach is anticipated for other TMSs with penetrating pores for post-lithium-ion batteries applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/bte2.20230033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-Stable Cycling of Organic Carboxylate Molecule Hydrogen Bonded with Inorganic Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene with Improved Redox Kinetics for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Battery Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">20230033</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Titanium dioxide (TiO2) has been widely investigated as a candidate for anode materials of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its low cost and high abundance.  However, the intrinsic sluggish ion/electron transfer rate hinders its practical applications for high energy d. storage devices.  In contrast, antimony (Sb) shows high specific theor. capacity (660 mAh/g) as well as excellent electron cond., but the large vol. variation upon cycling usually leads to severe capacity fading.  Herein, with the objective of achieving high-performance sodium storage anode materials, TiO2@C-Sb nanotablets with a small amt. of Sb content (6.4 wt%) are developed through calcination Ti-metal-org. framework (MIL-125) derived TiO2@C/SbCl3 mixt. under reductive atm.  Benefitting from the synergetic effect of well-dispersed Sb nanoparticles as well as robust porous TiO2@C substrate, the TiO2@C-Sb shows enhanced electron/ion transfer rate and predominantly pseudocapacitive sodium storage behavior, delivering a reversible capacity of 219 mAh/g at 0.5 A/g even after 1000 cycles.  More significantly, this method may be commonly used to incorporate other alloy-based high-theor. materials into MIL-125-derived TiO2@C, which is promising for developing high-energy-d. TiO2-based energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="93187ee97b70075b-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1020</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1035</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41578-021-00324-w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fundamentals, status and promise of sodium-based batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Usiskin, Robert; Lu, Yaxiang; Popovic, Jelena; Law, Markas; Balaya, Palani; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Maier, Joachim</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Reviews Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1020-1035</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRMADL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2058-8437</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Portfolio</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A Review.  Na-based batteries have shown substantial progress in recent years and are promising candidates for mitigating the supply risks assocd. with Li-based batteries.  In this Review, Na and Li batteries are compared in terms of fundamental principles and specific materials.  Principles for the rational design of a Na battery architecture are discussed.  Recent prototypes are surveyed to demonstrate that Na cells offer realistic alternatives that are competitive with some Li cells in terms of performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/s41560-022-01033-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Interfacial Engineering to Achieve an Energy Density of over 200 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> in Sodium Batteries</span>. <i>Nat. However, their energy d. is still lower than that of Li-based batteries.  Here we report an initial anode-free Na battery with an energy d. of over 200 Wh kg-1, which is even higher than that of the com. LiFePO4||graphite battery.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a promising candidate for large scale energy storage systems due to their low cost and reasonable performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Generally, the metal sulfide itself has poor cond., and the vol. expansion occurs when it is converted with sodium, which will destroy the integrity of the electrode structure, resulting in poor cycle performance and rate performance. Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) integrate several advantages such as adjustable pore sizes, large sp. surface areas, controllable geometrical morphol., and feasible surface modification.  Benefiting from these appealing merits, MOFs have recently been extensively explored in the field of advanced secondary batteries.  However, a systematic summarization of the specific functional units that these materials can act as in batteries as well as their related design strategies to underline their functions has not been perceived to date.  Motivated by this point, this review dedicates to the elucidation of diverse functions of MOFs for batteries, which involve the electrodes, separators, interface modifiers, and electrolytes.  Particularly, the main engineering strategies based on the phys. and chem. features to enable their enhanced performance have been highlighted for the individual functions.         </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped hollow carbon nanospheres (NHCS) with mesoporous carbon shells is selected as nanoreactors and encapsulated with few-layered MoS2 nanosheets to monitor its electrochem. properties and structural conversion in long-term cycling.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Recently, hydrogen energy has been significantly investigated by numerous technologies.  To date, noble platinum group metals have often been employed to fabricate working electrodes for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  Therefore, the demand of highly active HER catalysts based on effective and lower-cost materials is becoming more and more crit.  Transition metal dichalcogenide (TMD) materials could be one of the most suitable materials for these requirements because they possess numerous unique mech., electronic, and chem. characteristics that are greatly beneficial for HER processes.  Among many TMD materials, tungsten disulfide (WS2) and molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) are the most well-known TMD materials which have been intensively studied for different applications, including HER, batteries, and super capacitors.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Phase transition engineering, with the ability to alter the electronic structure and physicochem. properties of materials, has been widely used to achieve the thermodynamically unstable metallic phase MoS2 (1T-MoS2), although the complex operating conditions and low yield of previous strategies make the large-scale fabrication of 1T-MoS2 a big challenge.  Herein, we report a facile electron injection strategy for phase transition engineering and fabricate a composite of conductive TiO chem. bonded to 1T-MoS2 nanoflowers (TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs) on a large scale.  The underlying mechanism anal. reveals that electron-injection-engineering triggers a reorganization of the Mo 4d orbitals and results in a 100% phase transition of MoS2 from 2H to 1T.  In the TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs composite, the 1T-MoS2 demonstrates a higher electronic cond., a lower Na+ diffusion barrier, and a more restricted S release than 2H-MoS2.  In addn., conductive TiO bonding successfully resolves the stability challenge of the 1T phase.  These merits endow TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs electrodes with an excellent rate capability (650/288 mAh g-1 at 50/20 000 mA g-1, resp.) and an outstanding cyclability (501 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 700 cycles) in sodium ion batteries.  Such an improvement signifies that this facile and scalable phase-transition engineering combined with a deep mechanism anal. offers an important ref. for designing advanced materials for various applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202303464"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electron Modulated and Phosphate Radical Stabilized 1T-Rich MoS<sub>2</sub> for Ultra-Fast-Charged Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv.
