        </div><div class="casAbstract">1T-phase MoS2 is a promising electrode material for electrochem. energy storage due to its metallic cond., abundant active sites, and high theor. capacity.  However, because of the habitual conversion of metastable 1T to stable 2H phase via restacking, the poor rate capacity and cycling stability at high current densities hamper their applications.  Herein, a synergetic effect of electron-injection engineering and at.-interface engineering is employed for the formation and stabilization of defected 1T-rich MoS2 nanoflowers.  The 1T-rich MoS2 and carbon monolayers are alternately intercalated with each other in the nanohybrids.  The metallic 1T-phase MoS2 and conductive carbon monolayers are favorable for charge transport.  The expanded interlayer spacing ensures fast electrolyte diffusion and the decrease of the ion diffusion barrier.  The obtained defected 1T-rich MoS2/m-C nanoflowers exhibit high Na-storage capacity (557 mAh g-1 after 80 cycles at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate capacity (411 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and long-term cycling performance (364 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at 2 A g-1).  Furthermore, a Na-ion full cell composed of the 1T-rich MoS2/m-C anode and Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode maintains excellent cycling stability at 0.5 A g-1 during 400 cycles.  Theor. calcns. are also performed to evaluate the phase stability, electronic cond., and Na+ diffusion behavior of 1T-rich MoS2/m-C.  The energy storage performance demonstrates its excellent application prospects.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.04.063"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abd Ei-Hady, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alshitari, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saad Al-Bogami, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">1T MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets with Extraordinary Sodium Storage Properties Via Thermal-Driven Ion Intercalation Assisted Exfoliation of Bulky MoS<sub>2</sub></span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>61</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">361</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">369</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

In addn., the amorphization and conversion mechanism during the sodiation/desodiation process of NiS2 are proposed after investigation by in situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) measurements of intermediate products at successive charge/discharge stages.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202107370"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Multicomponent Synergistic Effect of Sandwich Structure Hierarchical Nanofibers for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>18</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2107370</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing hierarchical micro/nanostructures as anodes for sodium ion batteries is an important approach for exploiting efficient energy storage devices.  Herein, sandwich structure hierarchical nanofibers composed of hollow carbon fibers as the substrate, and MoS2 as the interlayer with Co and/or ZnS nanoparticles anchoring in carbon skeletons as the outer shell (carbon nanofiber/MoS2/Co-ZnS⊂NC) are prepd. via a multistep reaction strategy.  Profiting from the unique hierarchical structure, abundant migration channels of Na+, and multicomponent synergistic effects, the rapid diffusion kinetics are ensured and the utilization of active materials is maximized. A discharge capacity of 182.5 mAh g-1 is retained even after 10 000 cycles at 10.0 A g-1 as well as a high rate capacity of 202.0 mAh g-1 up to 30 A g-1.  The optimal at. ratio of Co element is further verified by the kinetic anal.  The full-cells assembled with Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode provide a high capacity of 179.2 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 for 500 cycles.  Combining in situ and ex situ characterizations and theor. calcns., possible sodium storage mechanisms and the origin of superior electrochem. properties are revealed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202000741"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Heterostructure SnSe<sub>2</sub>/ZnSe@PDA Nanobox for Stable and Highly Efficient Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Achieving a mol. level understanding of surface performance of nanomaterials by modulating the electronic structure is important but challenging.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rational design of electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries with high flexibility is still challenging.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite high theor. specific capacity and uniform interlayer channel for accommodation of ions, poor cycling stability and rate capacity have been identified as crit. roadblocks to further development of MoS2-based lithium ion batteries (LIBs) or sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  In this study, few-at.-layered MoS2 hollow nanospheres with expanded interlayer spacing, due to alternate intercalation of N-doped monolayer carbon (m-C) between the adjacent MoS2 monolayers, have been designed and synthesized via an annealing-followed soft-template approach. For LIBs, the hollow nanospheres can also deliver a reversible discharge capacity of 1025 mA h g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 80 cycles. Through a facile multistep template-engaged strategy, ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets are grown on nitrogen-doped carbon-coated Cu2S nanoboxes to realize the Cu2S@carbon@MoS2 configuration.  The design shortens the diffusion path of electrons/Na+ ions, accommodates the vol. change of electrodes during cycling, enhances the elec. cond. of the hybrids, and offers abundant active sites for sodium uptake.  By virtue of these advantages, these three-layered Cu2S@carbon@MoS2 hierarchical nanoboxes show excellent electrochem. properties in terms of decent rate capability and stable cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1039/D2TA08777D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rational Design and Regulation of Tremella-Liked Selenium Doping MoS<sub>2</sub> for Highly Reversible Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1954</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1965</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D2TA08777D</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design and regulation of tremella-like selenium-doped MoS2 for highly reversible sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Ruiyu; Li, Shiying; Li, Lixiang; Liu, Chengxin; Liu, Xiaojie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1954-1965</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2), due to its high theor. specific capacity (670 mA h g-1), has evoked considerable investigation interest in the area of Na+ storage.  Nonetheless, the irreversible conversion of the original material MoS2 into Mo/Na2S during sodium insertion incurs rapid capacity degrdn.  Herein, to avoid this severe irreversibility, NayMoS2 is employed to replace the above irreversible products to facilitate subsequent sodium extn., achieving reversible transformation of the raw material.  In order to accomplish this goal, tremella-like hollow MoS2(1-x)Se2x-C (x = 0, 0.1, 0.25, 0.5) spheres are elaborately prepd. and then act as an appropriate anode material exhibiting good sodium storage capacity.  It is proved that doping with Se and regulating the cut-off voltage improve the layer spacing and bond strength, so that the Mo-S bond is maintained without irreversible change during the sodium storage process.  This work delivers a practical strategy to modify the energy storage ability via reversible transformation of the original material and proposes an appropriate Se doping amt., demonstrating effective measures for constructing a relevant advanced anode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202208291"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solvent Induced Activation Reaction of MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets within Nitrogen/Sulfur-Codoped Carbon Network Boosting Sodium Ion Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2208291</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.202208291</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solvent Induced Activation Reaction of MoS2 Nanosheets within Nitrogen/Sulfur-Codoped Carbon Network Boosting Sodium Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Guangsheng; Li, Lixin; Zhu, Kai; Yan, Jun; Wang, Guiling; Cao, Dianxue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2208291</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2, as a classical 2D material, becomes a capable anode candidate for sodium-ion batteries.  However, MoS2 presents a disparate electrochem. performance in the ether-based and ester-based electrolyte with unclear mechanism.  Herein, tiny MoS2 nanosheets embedded in nitrogen/sulfur-codoped carbon (MoS2@NSC) networks are designed and fabricated through an uncomplicated solvothermal method.  Thanks to the ether-based electrolyte, the MoS2@NSC shows a unique capacity growth in the original stage of cycling.  But in the ester-based electrolyte, MoS2@NSC shows a usual capacity decay.  The increasing capacity puts down to the gradual transformation from MoS2 to MoS3 with the structure reconstruction.  Based on the above mechanism, MoS2@NSC demonstrates an excellent recyclability and the specific capacity keeps around 286 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 5000 cycles with an ultralow capacity fading rate of only 0.0034% per cycle.  In addn., a MoS2@NSC Na3V2(PO4)3 full cell with ether-based electrolyte is assembled and demonstrates a capacity of 71 mAh g-1, suggesting the potential application of MoS2@NSC.  Here the electrochem. conversion mechanism of MoS2 is revealed in the ether-based electrolyte and significance of the electrolyte design on the promoting Na ion storage behavior is highlighted.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1002/bte2.20230001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanoemulsion-Directed Assembly of Hierarchical ZnS@C Nanospheres with Penetrating Pores for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Battery Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">20230001</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/bte2.20230001</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoemulsion-directed assembly of hierarchical ZnS@C nanospheres with penetrating pores for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Xiaowei; Zhuo, Sifei; Tian, Lidong; Qiao, Mingtao; Lei, Xingfeng; Zhang, Hepeng; Zhang, Qiuyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Battery Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20230001</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">BEANAC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2768-1696</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To follow up on the performance of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), transition metal sulfides (TMSs) have been developed as promising carbon alternatives for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Although attractive, it is still a great challenge to fulfill their capacity utilization with high cycling performance.  Herein, a nanoemulsion-directed method has been developed to control the spherical arrangement of ZnS-C units with both penetrating macropores from the center to the surface and inner mesopores distributed among the bulks.  With respect to ion diffusion, the penetrating macropores could serve as the built-in ion-buffer reservoirs to keep a steady flow of electrolyte, while the inner mesopores facilitate the ion diffusion across the whole bulks.  In terms of stability, the radical porous structure could work as self-supported vertical bones to accommodate the vol. change from both lateral and vertical sides.  Besides, the localized carbon distributed among the ZnS nanoparticles not only acts as binding agents to join the numerous ZnS nanoparticles but also endows the radical bones with effective electron transmission capability.  As a proof of concept, such hydrangea-like ZnS-C nanospheres deliver sodium storage performance with high-rate and long-cycling capability.  This nanoemulsion-directed approach is anticipated for other TMSs with penetrating pores for post-lithium-ion batteries applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1002/bte2.20230033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-Stable Cycling of Organic Carboxylate Molecule Hydrogen Bonded with Inorganic Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene with Improved Redox Kinetics for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Battery Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">20230033</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/bte2.20230033</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.cclet.2023.108186"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Embedding Antimony Nanoparticles into Metal–Organic Framework Derived TiO<sub>2</sub>@Carbon Nanotablets for High-Performance Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Chin. Chem. Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">108186</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cclet.2023.108186</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Embedding antimony nanoparticles into metal-organic framework derived TiO2@carbon nanotablets for high-performance sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yao, Tianhao; Li, Li; Wang, Hongkang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Chemical Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">108186</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CCLEE7</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1001-8417</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Titanium dioxide (TiO2) has been widely investigated as a candidate for anode materials of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its low cost and high abundance.  However, the intrinsic sluggish ion/electron transfer rate hinders its practical applications for high energy d. storage devices.  In contrast, antimony (Sb) shows high specific theor. capacity (660 mAh/g) as well as excellent electron cond., but the large vol. variation upon cycling usually leads to severe capacity fading.  Herein, with the objective of achieving high-performance sodium storage anode materials, TiO2@C-Sb nanotablets with a small amt. of Sb content (6.4 wt%) are developed through calcination Ti-metal-org. framework (MIL-125) derived TiO2@C/SbCl3 mixt. under reductive atm.  Benefitting from the synergetic effect of well-dispersed Sb nanoparticles as well as robust porous TiO2@C substrate, the TiO2@C-Sb shows enhanced electron/ion transfer rate and predominantly pseudocapacitive sodium storage behavior, delivering a reversible capacity of 219 mAh/g at 0.5 A/g even after 1000 cycles.  More significantly, this method may be commonly used to incorporate other alloy-based high-theor. materials into MIL-125-derived TiO2@C, which is promising for developing high-energy-d. TiO2-based energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i2">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Experimental and calculation details, additional characterizations of 1T-Ni-MoS<sub>2</sub> and 2H-MoS<sub>2</sub>, additional electrochemical measurements and additional DFT computations (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.nanolett.3c04208/suppl_file/nl3c04208_si_001.pdf">nl3c04208_si_001.pdf (1.12 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="93187ee97b70075b-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

    var infoCentralCapture = (function () {
      //Detect mobile device
      window.mobilecheck = function () {
        var check = false;
        (function (a) {
          if (
            /(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera m(ob|in)i|palm( os)?|phone|p(ixi|re)\/|plucker|pocket|psp|series(4|6)0|symbian|treo|up\.(browser|link)|vodafone|wap|windows ce|xda|xiino/i.test(

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

  </script>
</p>

        <script nonce="93187ee97b70075b-SJC">
var currentJournal = "Nano Letters";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
